Printed by I. R. for N. L. are to be sold at the VVestdoore of Paules. To my most esteemed and approued louing friend, Maister Iohn Bodenham, R. A. vvisheth all happines. SIR, for many causes best knowne vnto your selfe, and euer of me to bee acknowledged, it might be thought were no longer worthy of your loue, if shoulde not in some sort shew my selfe thankeful. Besides, this history or Theater of the little VVorld, SVO+IVRE, first challengeth your friendly patronage, by whose motion vndertooke it, and for whose loue am willing to vndergoe the heauy burden of censure. must confesse that it might haue beene written with more maturitie, deliberation, but in respect of my promise haue made this hast, how happy know not, yet good enough hope, if you vouchsafe your kinde approbation: which with your iudgement holde ominous, and as vnder which, Politeuphuia was so gracious. Very fitly is man compared to a tree, whose rootes are his thoughts, whose branches and leaues his wordes (which are sufficiently set forth in choicest Sentences Similitudes) the fruite whereof are his workes, now shewed in Examples. In these, as in a glasse, is to be seene the course of mans life, such presidents, as eyther may be followed for vertuous, or eschevved as vicious. In many of them, haue beene briefe, the better to assure consume memory, in others, somewhat prolixe, because would auoyde obscuritie. These all, how they want the high charactered stile and smooth phrase (which is the body of eloquence) together with my best endeuours, offer to your loue, that hath begot in me this labor, whose after studies shall bee imployed to nourish it, and continue my euer thankefull mind for the same, resting alwayes Yours most assured to commaund. THE auncient Phylosophers (courteous Reader) haue written of tvvo vvorlds, the great and the lesser, the first is eyther vniuersall, which Plinie and others haue described, or perticuler, which is deuided into Heauen, called Mundus Architypus Earth, which Strabo, Pomponius Mela and Solinus haue set forth. The little world is man, (so called of Aristotle for vvhom the greater vvorld was made. haue therefore called these lucubrations or rather collections, The Theater of the little world for that in it thou maist beholde the inward and outward parts of man, liuely figured in hys actions and behauiour. And albeit the persons alledge haue giuen place to nature, yet the same or the like accidents happen daily. Thys worke gathered out of diuers learned Authours, may not call mine, least it bee sayd; Tu quidem Neuio, vel multa si fateris, vel sinegas surripuisti. But howesoeuer this my labour shall be thought perfunctory idle; because it is but a collection the flowers of antiquities and histories; dooth it comprehend those seauen persons which haue euer been thought most subiects to be written of, as Kings, Knights Bishops, Iudges, Magistrates, Husbands theyr houses, Religious men in the churches. The profit that ariseth by reading epitomized histories is, to aemulate vvhich thou likest in others, and to right vse of theyr examples. If haue obserued the true method (which Plato calleth a fire sent from heauen) nor memory as it deserueth, pardon my default, and shew thy gentle acceptance (which is Genius Librorum the life of bookes) proue al, approue the best, which done, Tanquam Hercules in biuio, sequere aut vita Table of all the Authours Names contayned in this Booke. D. D. Areopagita Dion, Diodorus, Dodoneus Damascenus D. Laertius Dioschorides E. Eusebius Eutropius Euripides Erasmus Egesippus. Guido Gueuara Guichardine Grymaldus H. Hieronimus Hesiodus Hermes Homer Herodotus Horace Herodianus. GOD is called in the holy Scriptures by these names; Elohim, Elohah, El, Eli, Elion, Iehouah, Iah, Adonai, Shaddai, Zebaoth, which signifie his name, essence, power, omnipotencie. GOD is called Iehouah not only because he is, hath been, and shall bee, but for that in him we liue, moue, and haue our beeing. Iesus in the Greeke tongue is called Sother in Latine Sanator or Saluator euery name of these signifieth in our language a Sauiour, likewise Emanuell which is to say, God with vs; Alpha Omega the beginning and the ending. Iesus is the proper name of Christ and Christ his sirname, Iesus the name of his and diuinitie, Christ the name of his office and dignitie, from which we are denominated Christians, how vainely then doe the Iesuites call themselues from his proper name? God hath created man seuerall wayes; the first, without man and woman, as Adam out of the earth; the second, of man without woman, as Euah of Adams rib, the third, of man and woman, as we are now borne, the fourth and last, of a virgin without man, as Christ of the virgine Mary. GOD within the Arke, made quiet the Lyon with the Leopard, the VVolfe with the Lambe, the Beare with the Cowe, the Tygar with the Crocodile, the Horse with the Mare, the Dog with the Catte, the Foxe with Hennes, the Hounds with Hares, and so of all other beasts. Socrates, the schoolemaister of Plato, confessed one onely God, and was condemned to drinke poyson, for teaching that the heathen Gods which they worshipped in hys time, were but vanity. Aul. Gel. VVhen Plato wrote of any serious matter, he began his Letters in the name of one only God, and when otherwise, in the name of many gods. Orpheus who did write of the pluralitie of gods in his time to Musaeus, made recantation, saying, There is but one God. Cicero alledgeth one soueraigne god, Hermes Euripides, Sophocles, Epictetus, Hesiodus, Ouid, attribute the creation of the world, and all things therein to one God. Antisthenes was of opinion, that there vvere many popular gods, and but one true and naturall God, which is the Creator of al. persons, naming the first Holy the second Fidius the third and in their oathes they did commonly put Fidius in the midst, as vnder that name comprehending all the The auncient Romans called their Iupiter Optimus maximus to shew that his diuinity is before his omnipotencie. The Persians had two gods, the one good, Creator author of al goodnes, whom they called by the name of Truth the other wicked, author of all euill, resembling him to Darknes and Ignorance. The Tuscane wits are sharpe and waspish, God keepeth them vnder a Prince, the Switzers be a people of a contrary disposition, peaceable and quiet, he therefore giueth them liberty, the Venetians to be of a meane betwixt both, therefore hee permitteth to them a mixt or meane kind of gouernment. Euclides beeing demaunded many things touching God, aunswered: Other thinges know not, but of this am assured, that hee hateth curious persons. The Athenians banished Protagoras their cittie and Country, because in one of his bookes he called in question the dietie; and caused his bookes to be burned. Vpon the image of Senacharib in Egipt was written, Learne by me to feare God Pherecides an Assyrian, for contemning God, and godlines, was so consumed vvith lyce, that he fled for shame from the societie of men, and died miserably. Lucian, hauing professed Christianity vnder the Emperour Traian, fell away afterwardes, and became so prophane and impious, that hee mocked at Religion and diuinitie, hee was sirnamed Atheist, in the end he was torne in peeces with dogs. The Emperour Iustinian, continuing obstinate in the heresie of Pelagius, the wrath of God fell vpon him, and suddenly without any grudge or token of sicknes, hee was depriued of his sences, and became a foole, hee was so strooken, that his life and folly ended in one day. Iulian the Apostate, at his death cast vp his blood into the ayre, crying Vicisti Galilaee Augustus erected an Altar in the Capitoll, with this inscription, The altar of the first begotten sonne of God. The Emperour Tiberius, vpon a Letter written to him from Pontius Pilate, reporting the miracles of Iesus and his innocent death, with his glorious resurrection, preferred a bill to the Senate with his assent vnto it, to haue them proclaime Iesus to bee God, which they refused, but Tiberius abode still in his opinion. Alexander the sonne of Mammea, dyd in his chappell worship Iesus, sirnamed Christ, of whom he tooke his Poesie, Doe not to another, that which thou wouldest not haue doone vnto thy selfe. And therefore the Antiochians called him the Arch priest of Syria. Certaine Pagans vsed outrage and offered great iniurie to a religious man, and in disdaine asked him what profit hee had by his Christ? Is not this, aunswered hee, a singuler profit, not to be moued with your bitter words, and to pardon the heauie wrongs you haue doone me? Cassianus. The Apostles forsooke all, and followed Christ, that the mother Church might receiue them naked, whom their mother flesh had brought naked into the world. The Christian souldiers vnder Iulian the Apostate burning incense, had almost forsaken Christ, but after, beeing better aduised, they restored theyr gifts to him which hee gaue them to commit idolatry, and earnestly desired, that for their right hand vvhich had made that fault, their whole body might suffer for Christ. Marcellius Bishop of Rome, for of Dioclesian offered sacrifice to idols, Heathen gods, but afterward lamented it. Origen constrained and drawne to the Altar by the cruell instruments of sathan, sacrificed to the gods of Alexandria, but after being desired to teach at Ierusalem, reading the psalme, Vnto the vvicked sayd God, what hast thou to doe, to declare mine ordinaunces, that thou shouldest take my commaundement in thy mouth? he sate downe and mourned. The Valentinians did hold, that there were thirtie couple of Gods, the Heathen vvorshipped thirty thousand. Euphemera Tegeian, wrote the true Historie and genealogie of the Heathen Gods, shewing that they were Kings, Princes, and great personages, and therfore he was called Atheist. Varro, the best learned of all the Romans, made a bedrole of all the gods, for feare (as he sayth) least they should stray away, wherin he concludeth, that those doe worship the true God, which adorne the onely one, and acknowledge him to bee the Gouernour of all the world. The Pyrrhonists, a kinde of Philosophers called Sceptikes (that is to say, doubters) dyd rather suspend theyr iudgment touching the then call it in question. Heauen is called of Aristotle, the most excelent booke of nature, whose longitude is between both the Poles, latitude from East to the VVest, and altitude from the South to the North. Epiphania containeth three orders, Seraphins, Cherubins, Thrones the first of these excelleth in zealous loue, the second in knowledge, the third in iustice. Epiphonomia containeth likewise three orders, Principalities, Powers, Dominations, the first teacheth men of lower estate to reuerence their farre betters; the next, chase away euill spirits, comforting the~ that fight in ghostly battel, the last informe me~ how to behaue the~selues in spiritual conflicts. Euphumia hath also vnder it three lower orders, Vertues, Archangels, Angels, Angels working miracles, shewing miracles, comforters. Saint Denis writeth of three Hierarchies, the first aboue heauen, of three persons, the second in heauen, of Angels, the third vnder heauen, of Prelates. The Spheare, taken generally, containeth all perfect rounde bodies, vvhether they be sollid or not; vvhether contained vnder one only Superficies or more, and so may euery Orbe be called a Spheare: perticulerly taken, and in his proper signification, nothing is a Spheare but a perfect round body being solid, contained vnder one Superficies or face, in whose middle is a poynt, from which all lines that are drawne to the Superficies, are equall the one to the other. This is deuided into two parts, Elementall which containeth the foure Elements, Fire, Ayre, VVater, Earth, which are subiect to alterations; Aethereall that compasseth the ementall substance in his hollownes· being by nature lightsome, vnchangeable, tenne Spheares. The first and highest, is called the first Mooueable containing all the other, and by his naturall motion mooueth from the East to the VVest, so to the East againe in The next is the heauen Christaline vvhich naturally but very slowlie, moueth from the East towards the vvest, in many yeeres passing but one degree. This motion hath caused the starres to alter their longitudes. The third is the Firmament of fixed starrs, whose motion by nature is vppon two little Circles, the one about the head of Aries the other of Libra which is called the motion of Trepidation The other seauen Spheares are of the seauen Planets, of which Saturne is the highest, yet slowest in proper motion, cold, dry, and pale, who endeth his course in thirty yeeres, he mooueth from vvest toward East. Iupiter is temperate, faire and bright, moouing from VVest to East, vvhose course preformed in twelue yeeres. Mars is hote and dry, of fierie colour making his reuolution from VVest toward East in two yeeres. Sol is a King among the Plants in the of his throne, the golden eye of heaue~, lightning the vniuersall frame with his beames making one perfect reuolution in three hundred sixtie fiue dayes and sixe houres. Venus is cold, moist, and cleere, her is like vnto Sol neuer aboue eight fortie degrees from him, when she sheweth in Horizon shee is called Lucifer the day starre and when shee followeth him, shee is called Hesperus the euening starre. degrees from the Sun· his course is like vnto the same. The Moone lowest of the seauen, running ouer the whole Zodiacke in Al these seauen make theyr reuolution naturally fro~ VVest to East, yet by violence of the first moueable, are carried from East to VVest. The Spheare of heauen goeth vpon two Poles, the North and the South, which are neuer seene of vs. The Center of the Spheare is the middle poynt of the same, and the Axe of it is a right line, passing from one side of the same (by his Center) to the co~trary side, about which the roundnes of heauen moueth, as a wheele about an Axletree, but the lyne it selfe still. The ends of this line Axis are called Cardines caeli because they mooue about the hollownes of the Poles. The Hemispheare is halfe the Spheare, that is the part that is seene of vs, for default of our sight, it seemeth to vs to touch the earth. In the body of the highest Spheare first Moueable, it is imagined that there are ten Circles, the sixe greater are the Aequinoctial, Zodiacke, Horizon, Meridian and two Colures the lesser foure, are the Tropicke of Cancer the Tropicke of Capricorne the Articke and Antarticke The Equinoctiall, called the Aequator or girdle of heauen, deuideth Heauen into two parts alike, the which be called Hemispheares so called, eyther for that it is equally in the midst of heauen, or for that the Sun co~ming to his circle, makes both day night equall. The Zodiacke is a great circle, taketh his name of the Greek word signifying a lyuing creature, and of the Latines Signifer for th Horizon deuideth the halfe of the which we see, from the halfe which vvee not, in Latine it is called Finitor maketh principal points, East, VVest, North, The Meridian passeth fro~ the Poles of world by our Verticall poynt, cutting the Hrizon in the North and South poynts. Colures doe declare the times called Aequnoctiall and Solstitiall that is, when the and night be equall in length, also when day and the night are at the longest, by the signe Libra into Aries turne to their owne point. The Tropicke of Cancer is a circle, equall distant from the Equinoctiall lying it and the North Pole, and touching the in the beginning of Cancer it is Tropicke signifying a returning, because Sunne beeing brought to this point, in his noone height, and returneth againe. The Tropicke of Capricorne is betwixt the Aequator and the South Pole, is described by the Sun in the shortest day of vvinter, which time the sun entereth into Capricorne The Articke Circle is a lesse circle of the Spheare, described by the Northerne Pole, of the Ecliptick· Proclus sayth it is described by the formost foote of Vrsa maior thereof taketh his name. The Antarticke is a like circle described by the South Pole of the Eclipticke and is called Antarticke of a Greek word, which signifieth Opposition because it is opposite to the other. The foure greater circles are still the same through the whole world, and are sayd to bee moueable circles, for so much as in the motion of heauen, they be also mooued, of the which the Aequinoctiall and the Zodiacke are moueable perfectly: but the two Colures are vnperfectly mooueable, and neuer shew the whole circle in any crooked Spheare. greater circles be called fixed, for that they neuer mooue by the motion of heauen, but they be changeable in euery region, forsomuch as the Verticall of euery Region is diuers, by the which the Meridian of necessitie must passe, and is the Pole also of the Horizon By the twelue signes the Planets that bee called Sidera errantia moue not, for they err, for they haue most certaine moouing, but they bee called errantia because they holde theyr course against the course of the Firmament. Caput Draconis and Cauda Draconis the of the Dragon, and the tayle, are two starre that are of the natures of Planets; this kept the garden of the Hesperides for his continuall vvatching vvas placed Heauen. Cepheus was sometimes King of Egipt, husband of Cassiopeia and Father of Andrmeda the loue of Perseus at whose byrth Gods swore that none of his kinde should tast of immortalitie, and therefore hee stellified. Bootes or the Northerne VVagoner, the two Beares, the same circle is and is beautified vvith starres. Corona or Ariadnes crowne, made of ni siluer starres, which was the garland that Ve+nus gaue vnto her when she became loue after that Theseus forsooke her. Hercules after his many great labours, the consent of all the Gods, vvas taken into Heauen. Lyra or the Harpe of Orpheus by vvho melodious touch hee drevve stones, byrds and beasts after him; after his death fained to be a signe in Heauen. Cignus the Swanne, vnder whose shape Iupiter rauished Laeda was by him made a star. Cassiopeia sometimes the pride of Egypt, for brauing the Sea Nymphs Nereides with her beauty, was changed into a starre, vvho in the motion of the heauens is drawn backwards. Perseus is next her, the sonne of Danae who~ Iupiter begot of her in the shape of a golden shower, he ouercame Medusa by the help of Minerua and rescued Andromeda but at hys returne, his grandsire Acriseius meeting him, vvas by Medusas heade turned to a stone, which Perseus much lamenting, was by the Gods taken vp into heauen. Auriga or the VVagoner, the Poets fayne to be Hippolitus who stying his mother Phaedras lust, was for his chastitie by the Gods made a starre. By him stands the great Iupiters Nurse, by hee vvas fostered, vvhen hee vvas conueied by his mother Ops from Saturne who would haue deuoured him. Serpentarius the Serpent holder, hauing the picture of a man, is composed of foure starres, holding a Serpent in his and as it vvere striuing hee is fayned to bee Esculapius the sonne of Apollo vvho vvhen Hippolitus vvas dead, restored him againe to life, and after was called Vibius. The Serpent Phoebus placed by his sonne for that by his meanes hee restored king Minos sonne from death to life. Sagitta the dart, is that strong steeled with the which Hercules killed the Griffi that tyred vpon Prometheus hart, when was chained to the top of Caucasus for steling fire from heauen. Aquila the Eagle, or the bird of Ioue wh stole the fayre Phrygian Ganimede brought him to Iupiter who serued him Nar and Ambrosia. The Dolphin is that Fish vvhich when rion was cast into the sea, first receiue him kindly vppon his backe, and sette him on shoare in Italie, in vvhereof, the Gods placed him in firmament. Equiculus the little horse of Bacchus vvhom he vsed to ryde vvhen his idle vvas ouerburdened vvith too much vvhose death, his maister desired the Gods that he might in requitall of his be made a starre. Pegasus the flying horse, ingendred by the sun, of Medusas blood, could be managed by vntill Bellerophon vndertooke him, who ding vp into the skies, fell downe from him to the Seas, but the horse kept his way still heauen, where he resteth. Andromeda the wife of Perseus (at whose rth the Gods promised her immortality,) ter her death had her place amongst the arres. The Triangle signifieth the three squared forme of the thrice happy land of Cicilia, the Countrey of Ceres, which shee desired the Gods to be placed in heauen, for the loue she re to the Land. All these stars aboue mentioned, haue their residence in the Arcticke clymes, keeping their continuall motion with the Spheares. Aries is the golden Ramme, that carryed Phryxus and his sister ouer Hellespont from their cruell mother. Taurus the Bull that Iupiter transformed him into, when he stole Europa the daughter of Agenor VVithin his forme are the seauen starres: once Atlas daughters called Atlantides, of which Electra the fayrest, the same night that Troy was burned, puld in her head, and would not see the flames, since vvhich me, there be but sixe of them seene, vvho are also named, Hyades and Plyades Gemini, Castor and Pollux were begot Iupiter one Leda when he transformed into a Swan. Cancer the Crab, when Hercules was with Hydra bit him by the heele, he espying killed, but Iuno for that she se her, made her a signe in heauen. Leo was the Nemean Lyon, whom Hercul slew, and Ioue placed in heauen to grace Sonne. Virgo the Poets faine to be Iustice, vvh forsaking earth flew to heauen, enforced the wickednes of men. Libra are the ballance of Iustice, she wayed the vnequall actions of mens lyfes. Scorpio was made a signe for killing Ori with his sting, who proudly boasted, that earth bred no monster, but he could subdue Sagitarius is Crocus, the sonne of Euthmia that nursed the Muses, who sucked milke the Muses left, whom at their reque Capricornus was the disguised shape of the God of sheepheards, halfe fish and half Goate, when the Gyant Typhon warred the Gods, which when the wars ended, Iupiter placed among the starres. Aquarius is Ganymedes of Troy, vvhom Iupiter caused his Eagle to fetch to bee his ge. Pisces are those fishes, that vvhen Venus and Cupid sporting themselues by were compassed by the great Gyant Tiphon for feare of him tooke the Riuer, and were sustained by them whom she changed to starres. The VVhale is placed next to the signes, which should haue deuoured Andromeda Orion was the sonne of Hyreus who entertained Iupiter, Neptune and Mercury as they trauailed, who desired of them a Sonne, who after his death was thus metamorphized. Eridanus or Padus the Riuer wherein Phaethon was drowned, which for quenching of that flame, is among the starres. The Hare is at his feete vvith two fierce dogges pursuing it, this fearefull beast Phaethon delighted in, when he liued. Iasons shippe in the which hee brought to Colchos, the golden fleece was placed next to Orion The Crow was so changed by Apollo and the Cup likewise, with Hydra the told him, kept him from the vvell, he was sent with the Cup for water. Centaurus called Chiron the of Esculapius, Achilles and Hercules was the Gods stellified. The VVoolfe was placed next to him, an Altar, holding the Sacrifice in his ready to offer, signifying his deuotion. The wheele whereon Ixion was tortured for offering dalliance to Iuno The Southerne fish is called Venus so transformed in the Sea. From the beginning of the creation of world, Abell and Cain did religiously God, but Enoch was the first that set downes what manner he should be called vpon. THE auntient Romaines through the of nature onely, did so reuerenth think of Religion, that they sent theyr chidren, and the most noble men of Rome Sonnes into Hetruria, to learne the mann of seruing God. They had neuer any greater meanes to extend the borders of theyr Empire, and the glory of their famous Acts ouer all the earth, then Religion. Among the Athenians no King was created, before he had taken orders, and vvas a Priest, they killed all those that enuied theyr religion. Theyr chiefest oath was this, In defending religion, both alone and with others will fight against my foes. The Aegiptians of Philosophers chose their Priests, and of Priests their Kings. The Lacedemonians when they laid hands vpon those that fled to the temple of Neptune for succour, Sparta was so shaken vvith that few of theyr houses escaped. The Phocians were condemned in a great summe of money, by the Amphyctiones, because they had tilled grounde, which was consecrated to the Gods, which sum, when they refused to pay, they pronounced theyr Countrey, as confiscate to the Gods, wherevpon arose a warre, called the holy vvarre, made by the rest of the Grecians against the~, which in the end was their ruine. Epicurus first began to rise, against the religion of God. The Germaines in the time of Tacitus, neyther lawe nor religion, nor knowledge nor forme of common wealth, whereas they giue place to no nation for good in all things. The Chananites were the first that vve ignorant of the true worshipping of God because theyr first Authour and original Cham vvas cursed of his Father Noah. The Hebrewes vvorshipped the true at the first, but when they increased in number, as the sands of the Sea, they went into diuers Countries, and left there true religion, fayning newe Gods and ceremonies· after their owne inuentions. The Romaines allowed the seruice of Gods, and to that end builded a temple to them all, called Pantheon, yet vvould they neuer receaue the true God, to wit, Iehouah the Lord GOD of the Hebrewes. Ecebolius in Constantines time a Christian, in Iulianus a Gentile, lay along in the Church Porch, crying, tread me vnder foote, for that am vnsauory salt. Vitalis a Souldiour, when Vrsicinus a Phisition endured martirdome for religion, seeing his courage to faile, boldly spake to him, not Vrsicinus now cast away thy selfe, that hast cured so many, nor after so much blood of thine spilled, loose the merrit which is prepared for thee. The vnchristianlike behauiour of Christians, haue caused the Turks euen to detest the true religion. The cruelty, blasphemy, and couetousnes of the Spanyards, haue altogether alienated the poore Indians from the religion, which they gaue out to be true. The Princes of Italy support the Iewes, rank enemies to religion. Constantine was the first of the Romaine Emperours, that forsaking errors and heresies, confessed and adored the maiesty of the true God. Iouianus refused to gouern those that were not sound in faith; (saith he) that am a Christian, cannot become your Emperour, that are the Disciples of Iulian a runnagate from Christ. The liberality of Princes, and especially of Matilda a Dutches of Italy, who at her death made the Pope her heire, begot ambition in the Bishops of Rome, and ambition destroyed religion. Gratianus at his first entering, finding a places full of Arrians, the lawes of Valen his Vncle making for them, fearing some generall tumult, if he should presently so manie, gaue leaue that euerie religion might haue churches Oratories with but being once ioyned with Theodotius, hee commanded that all theyr should be depressed; He sent the confession of his faith to Saint Ambrose. Lycurgus reformed the estate of the Lacedemonians, Numa Pompilius of the Romaines, Solon of the Athenians, and Deucalion of all the Grecians, generally by making them deuoute and affectionate toward the Gods in prayers, oaths, oracles, and prophecies, through the meanes of feare, and hope of the diuine nature, which they imprinted in them. Alexander after hee had sacked Tyrus, marched towards Ierusalem, to destroy it, because the Iewes refused to ayde him with victuals and munition, but when hee saw the high Priest comming towards him attired in his holy garments, he so reuerenced him, that he not onely spared the Citty, but also gaue gifts to the temple. Cains a Romaine Emperor sent Petronius Syria with commandement, to bid bate to the Iewes; If they would not receiue Image into their temple, which they to doe They had rather dye then from the lawes of God. The King of Calecut is chiefe of his religion and for this cause goeth before the other of India in dignity, and is called Samory, that is to say, God on earth Canutus not full yeres before the const, apparently proueth, that Princes kept their authority to co~mand, for matters of more then Charles the great, to Christian religion at Padua in Italy, and Paris in France erected Academies. Xerxes through counsaile of his Magi, commaunded all the temples and churches Greece to bee burned, saying, it was wicked impious, that Gods should but vp in Churches. Theodectes a Poet, mingled his Tragedies holy Scriptures, therefore was with blindnes, vntill he had recanted his piety. Iew often baptized for money sake, came to Paulus the Nouatian Bishop to that end, but the vvater twice vanishing out of the Fount, he said, man, eyther thou dissemblest egregiously, or else thou art baptized vnwillingly. The Maker and Redeemer of the world, vse great measure in all things, except in praying, wherein hee was alwayes long, which he shewed most cleerely in Gethsemany, where much the more the agonie did oppresse him, much the more did he enlarge his prayers. and Psalme, and the next sixe following the great Alleluya, vvhich the Apostles sayd grace at Easter and Pentecost. The first earthly man of the Hebrewes, called Adam, as homo tanquam ex humo other heauenly of the Chaldeans, Enoch which signifieth true man, or that man hath vndertaken, and hopeth to call God. Iacobus minor the sonne of Ioseph of Christ, was so like him, that in the for feare they should mistake, Iudas him a kisse; his knees with continuall became as hard as a Cammels hoofe. Bartholomew the Apostle, by his prayers, the destracted daughter of King of India, to her former sences. Arcadius was called of Chrisostome, the Christian and godly Prince, who a litle his death wone estimation of holines, without the admiration of a great saued from destruction by his prayers. God gaue Narsetes victory, more through zealous prayers that he vsed, then his and valour; he neuer went to Sea, nor any battaile, nor determined of warre, mounted on horseback, but first he went the temple and serued God. The Emperour Heraclius, after his warres ended, entered Constantinople, sitting a Chariot without ornaments, and openly thanks to the Sonne of God for his victories. Tiberius that vertuous Emperour, being to a blessed necessity, as he walked in midst of his Pallace, he saw at his feete a stone, vvhich was in forme of the crosse; and because he thought it religious to spurne it with his feete, he caused it to be taken vp, and vnder that found another, and so a third of the same forme, which when that was taken vp, there was found two millions of Duckets, for the which he thanked God. Marcus Aurelius hauing felt the helpe of Christian prayers, ceased his persecution. Prayers are of the Poets fayned, to be the daughters of Iupiter, because Kings great men haue a number of followers and sutors. Apollo being praied vnto to sing an Him to the great GOD, began vvith this verse, VVhich made the first man and called him Adam. The lessons of Pythagoras, Plato, and Disciples, began and ended with prayers. The Brachmans among the Indians, Magi among the Persians, neuer began any thing without praying vnto God. Cleanthes in his Iambicke verses, God to vouchsafe to guide him by his cause, which guideth all things in order, the which cause he calleth destiny, and the cause of causes. Pray said Nestor to his children, for vnlesse God helpe vs, we shall all perish. The Romaines after many great victories, to make a very rich crowne of and offer it to Apollo, but the common being poore, the vvomen defaced Owches and Iewels to make it with all, which, they had graunted three things to on their heads, garlands of flowers, to goe in chariots, and openly to the feasts of Gods. Theseus asked of the Gods three things, good fortune, want of inward sorrow, such glory as was neither false, counterfaite, nor of three other boones which he prayed of Neptune, the third was, in his fury his sonne Hyppolitus, and wishing his violent death, which after it was granted, he repented him. Demonides hauing crooked feet, lost both of his shooes, he desired God his shoone might serue his feet that had them. VVhen Alcibiades was condemned by the Athenians, they commaunded the religious people of either sexe to curse him, which one of them refused to doe, saying, that they had entered religion not to make vniust, but iust prayers. Sylla, Tiberius, Caligula, and Nero, could but commaund and kill, on the other side, Augustus, Titus, and Traianus, could not but pray and pardon, in such manner that they ouercame praying, as the other fighting. The Lacedemonians custome was, not to craue any thing of their Gods, but what was of importance and consequence, saying all smal matters were to be obtained by industry. Plinie in an oration he made in the prayse of Traiane, commended the custome of the Auntients, to make inuocation before the beginning of their work, and sayd, that there could be no assured nor wise beginning of any enterprise, without the especiall ayde and counsaile of God. In Athence was a temple dedicated to Mercy, which the Athenians kept so well watched and locked, that without leaue licence of the Senate, none might enter therein; in this temple were only the Images of pittiful men, and none entered there to pray and doe sacrifice, but those that vvere pittifull Macrobius. Isocrates prayed God to saue and keepe him from his friends, rather then his enemies, saying, of his enemies he could be wary, trust them not, so can not of my iends, because haue assured confidence them. Octauius prayed GOD that it might be that by him the common wealth of was preserued from all danger, and at death to carry with him that hope, that might remaine many ages in that estate left it. poore man craued an almes of the Maximilian, and told him, that they both of one Father, to wit, Adam, and consequently were brethren, desiring to deale with him: to whom the gaue a small peece of siluer, whereat he saw the poore man discontented, he told him, that he ought to take it in good worth, saying that if euery one of his would giue him as much, he should be richer then himselfe. Anthony distressed by the King of Paria, held vp his hands to heauen, saying, if disdaine of GOD remayned of his fortunes, hee desired it might fall vpon so the Romaine army might be freed, haue the victory. Virginia the daughter of Virginius, for that her Father was a Plebeian, was forbidden to doe sacrifice with other Romaine matrone in the temple of Chastity, wherfore she a temple of her own house to the Goddesse· for which, the Senate made her a Liuius. Claudius defiled the faire matrone Obena, as he found her praying in the temple Minerua, who condemned for sacriledge, escaped punishment by bribes. Brutus not satisfied in killing Caesar, his prayers vnto Iupiter, and the hoast heauen, to plague Caesar and his posterity. VVhen the Cretans were vngently intreated of the Romaines, they did not pray their Gods to send them pestilence, warre and famine, or sedition, but that they suffer new customes, manners, and fashion to be brought amongst them. The praier of old Cato, was that the cou of pleas might bee set with linnes and to take the professors of the braw study of law. Alexander caused his Horse Bucephalus be buried; Augustus his Parrot; and Heliogabalus his Sparrow· at whose hee prayed and caused the body to be embalmed. The Hebrewes, by reason of the tenne boasted that they had the cheefest and the summe of all Vertue. MArcus Marcellus building a Temple which he called the Temple of Honor, so place situate the same, as none could any entrance therein, except hee came rough the Temple of Vertue. The Romans did not onely assigne the places to men of vertue, but likewise they gaue them Speares, and Garlands. VVhen the Romaine Victors rode in a slaue sate behind them striking them vpon the necke, that they shoulde themselues and not be proude, and euery man shoulde hope by vertue to to the like dignity. Fabius for his vertues was sirnamed Maxius where before he was called Gurges It is recorded of Fabius, that it was as hard draw him from his honestie and vertues, as the sunne from his course. Camillus, for a disgrace happening to him in Rome, was banished into Campania where his vertues and seruice in the vvars that country succeeded so happily with him· that hee returned to Rome not as an offender, but in great tryumph. Socrates made him to weepe, for that hee shewed him by liuely reasons that he vvas lesse estimation then a base hinde if hee not vertue, and that it behooued him to sorrowfull. The Rhodians and the Lydians had a lawe that those sonnes which followed not they fathers in theyr vertues, but liued viciously should be disinherited, and theyr lands giue to the most vertuous of that race, not admitting any impious heyre Varro. For that Artaxerxes Mnemon was a vertuous Prince delighted in peace, the succeeding kings of Persia were called by his name· Basilius, Emperour of Constantinople, his death exhorted Leo his sonne to vertuous actions, and not to become slaue to owne affections; by good lyfe and studie to beautifie his soule, shewing himlfe the image and Lieuetenant of the Knig heauen. Demetrius, the scholler of Theophrastus, he had ten yeeres gouerned the state of hauing in memory of his vertues, ree hundred and threescore statues erected Greece, yet were they all through enuie dovvne, which when he heard of, he Though they burne my pictures, yet cannot ey burne the vertuous cause of them. Alexander vvilled that the Grecians and Barbarians shoulde no more be disguised by eyr garments, but that the Grecian should be knowne by vertue, and the Barbarian by accounting all vertuous men and all vicious Barbarians. Menander King of the Bactrians, vvas so beloued of his subiects for his vertues, after his death the principall citties conded which of them shoulde haue the of his buriall; for the appeasing of which it was concluded that each of them remembrance of his worthynes) should a tombe. Harmocrates the last Tyrant in Sicilia, at the very instant of his death exhorted hys sonne to liue so vprightly, that his vertues might make him to be enuied. Alexander praised greatly this vertue in the Phylosopher Calisthenes, that for others he asked many things, for himselfe nothing. Into the graue Senate of Areopage were receiued, except they had made some notable proofe of their vertues. rare example of a Romans vertue was who hauing Claudius in his custodie, who before had proscribed him, restored him to his estate, and preserued him fr danger. Iuno through her riches, Mercurie his eloquence, Venus through her beautie Ms through his threats, and the rest of Gods hauing all conspired against Iupiter were not able to pull him out of heauen: which the Poets signified, that a man can by no meanes be turned aside from iustice. Bookes or Dialogues which did all of vertue; in which that he might not be thought vngrateful toward his Maister Socrates, who woulde neuer write any thing, hee bringeth him in that which he heard him speake. Anacharsis led with the onely loue of left the kingdom of Scythia to his brother, trauailed into Grecia, where learned phylosophy of Solon. Pelopidas, generall of the Thebans, is more for his notable vertue hee shevved, he was prysoner in the hands of the tyrannous K. of the Phereans, the~ all his vertues gotten before. The Emperour Rodolphus, othervvise of parentage, by his vertues mounted to Monarchie. Maximilian the Emperour, aunswered one desired his Letters patents to ennoble am able to make thee rich, but vertue on must make thee noble Alexander Seuerus neuer kept in his court ill disposed persons, or suffered any ough neuer so neere to him in blood, once faulty, to escape vnpunished. Marius esteemed it a great poynt of vertue high courage, to bee skilful in cosenage. Two of the most famous Citties in the were in two extremeties, Rome the of vice, and Alexandria the end of all Betweene the two zodiacall signes, Leo and Libra, is a virgin called Astraea or Iustice, the which in times past dwelled vpon the earth, beeing abused and neglected of mortall men, tooke ber flight to heauen. THe Egyptians who vvere the Lawmakers, in theyr Citties caused to be paynted without handes, and the President or chiefe Iustice, with hys blindfolded, thereby signifying, that ought neither to be briber, nor respecter persons. Beza faineth Iustice and Mercie to bee two Sisters standing by the throne of God. VVhen the Hebrewes asked a King of Samuell, they added this, to iudge al nations Aristides, for his impartiall dealing in matters, was sirnamed the Iust. Mycerinus the son of Cleops, surpassed the Kings of Egipt for true iustice. Iunius Brutus, a consul of Rome, condemned his two sonnes Titus Tiberius to beeheaded, for that they conspired the reentre Tarquinius race into Rome. Philip and Alexander his sonne, when any to complaine, stopped one of theyr which they reserued for the No man durst euer solicite Cato Censorius any dishonest cause. The Emperour Iulian, though otherwise a condemned no man before his cause heard. Cambises commaunded Sisamnes skinne his iniustice to bee of, and couering iudgement seate appointed sonne to iudge in his place. Seleucus, Gouernour of his sonne taken in adultery, whose punishment losse of both his eyes, to satisfie iustice, in some sort the people, who intreated to remit the punishment, caused one of sonnes, and another of his owne to bee out. boy was condemned at Athence for that vsed to catch young Quailes and to pull theyr eyes· and so to let them flie againe, the Areopagites thought not vvorthy lyue, fearing that if hee were remitted for offence, hee would not stick in time to attempt greater cruelties. Phocion refused to helpe his sonne in lavv Charillus in iudgement, beeing accused for bribery, saying withal, that he had made him his allie in al iust reasonable matters only. Philip was importuned by an olde woman to heare her cause, to whom when the King made aunswer that he had no leysure, she replyed, then be no King; which he wel regarding, sette all busines aside to heare her complaint. Thys King beeing once ouertaken sleepe, and not well hearing the defence of Machetas, he condemned him in a certaine summe, wherevpon cryed out, appeale to Philip when hee is awake vvhich when he heard againe he aquited him. Philip the first King of Macedon, slaine by Pausanias a meane gentleman, because hee woulde not let him haue iustice Antipater. VVhen Aristides was to determine a controuersie betweene two, one of them sayde, My aduersary Aristides hath doone the wrong. But he aunswered; My friend, declare onely vvherein he hath wronged thee for am here to doe thee right, and not my lfe. Laertius. Antonius Venereus, Duke of Venice, caud his sonne to die in prison because hee had uished a maide. Papinian a Pagan, although hee was by the Emperor Caracalla (whose and familiar hee was) to defende an cause, would not doe it. Cleon of Lacedemon, minding to deale in affayres, called all his friends and told them that hee renounced and himselfe of all friendship, because caused men sometimes to swarue from Aurelianus the Emperour, was so fearefull of placing an vnwoorthy man in the seate of iudgement, that hee neuer preferred any to the dignity of Senator, but with the consent of the whole Senate. Traianus allighted from his horse as he was going to warres, onely to doe iustice to a poore woman. Mardus sate in iudgement vpon his Sonne Cartanes, and would haue put him to death, but Artaxerxes seeing his iustice, pardoned his sonne. Agesilaus requested by his Father to gyue sentence against equity, graciously denyed him with this aunswer; You haue taught Father, from my youth to obey the lawes, therefore will now obey you therein, by iudging nothing against the lawes. At Athence, if any man committed wilful murder, iudgeme~t was prosecuted in a place called Martius Pagus it against his vvill, the sessions was kept in Palladum if the murderer were apprehended, and the deede doo chaunce medly, in Delphico Domitius alwayes punished the poore, those that were of no power, but the rich and mighty he pardoned. Demetrius the besieger, hauing many requests and supplications of his subiects, threwe them all into the water as went ouer the bridge, wherupon his subiects conceiued such hatred against him, that Armie forsooke him yeelded to Pyrrhus· who draue him out of his kingdome. The Romaine Censors, disfranchised a cittizen of Rome, because he breathed yawned a little too loude in theyr presence. Augustus Caesar, beeing desired by Tacitus to come to his house, to iudge of an offence which one of his sonnes had committed, did Tacitus requested, but first he commaund that euery one should first set downe his in writing, and then he gaue his fearing that if he had spoken first, they all haue said as he sayd. Ferdinando the fourth, adiudging tvvo to death more through anger then stice, one of them cryed aloude, saying: King, we cite thee to appeare within yes before the tribunall seate of Iesus Christ, receiue iudgement for thine iniustice vpon last of which dayes he dyed. The name of law was vnknown among the Greekes in the time of Homer. Minos, Zoroastres, Trismegistus, Lycurgus, Solon, Draco, Numa, haue euer fathered theyr vpon some God, the better to haue in authoritie, nature teaching the~, that appertained vnto God alone, and that otherwise the lawes would not be obserued. The Princes of Persia Media, gaue to Darius, that hee shoulde neuer change law after it was once made. Diodorus writ of certaine people, among who~ no man ought to speake of the change of a lawe, except hee wore a halter, vvith vvhich hee was hanged if his opinion not place. The Cittizens of Marseills, were much renowned for that they remained constant their lawes customs without changing· Lycurgus, after hee had brought the Lacedemonians to receiue his lawes, hee ma them all sweare that they would alter no of them during his absence, and after neuer returned into his country againe. Orpheus was cut in peeces by the of Thrace, because hee had changed the lawes. The Emperour Galba was greatly praise because hee woulde neither change auncie law, nor create nevv. Plutarch exhorted Traiane to take mo care in seeing his auncient lawes vvell preserued then in making newe, and aboue things, that his life should serue for a law. Solon requested that his lawes might preserued for an hundred yeres space, to the ende that they might neuer be changed. In Greece were certaine Officers called who tooke great regard that no man should derogate from any good lawes. The Almaines vvere praysed for changing theyr customs, which were found to bee but before. VVhen Varus was vanquished in Germae, they put out the eyes of all the Lavvyers ich they could finde, and from some they lled out theyr tongues also. Galeaze Duke of Millan, caused a to be hanged for delaying of a sute ainst a manifest and cleere debt. Ferdinando the Emperour, sending a vice into the Indies which had beene newlie scouered, forbad him to carry ouer any vvith him, to the end hee should not we there the seede of sutes. in matters of tryall and lavve, so simply behaue themselues, that they icke to theyr first iudgement, neuer appeale further. Horace maketh me~tion of a statue of Mara, which none durst beholde that vndertooke not a iust cause. Astraea which maintained good lawes, and the equitie of them gaue quiet and to euery one, is nowe flowen to impatient of such iniquities. There was an ancient law in Rome, that no Bakers, Bruers, Butchers, or such like trades might be Senators. M. Caelius was saide to haue a good right hand, but an euill left, because he could plea better against a man then for him. The Romans and the Lacedemonians a law, that no man should sup when hee lyst nor with what he list. It was also a lawe among the Lacedemonians, that hee which had deliuered three to the co~mon wealth, should be from watching, both by day and night; which deliuered fiue, shoulde not be burdened with any publique office, so highly esteemed they procreation of chyldren. It was not lawfull for the Spartans to take fro~ their enemies any thing, no not so much as the booty or spoyle in war. Vlpitian the Lawyer, wrote the how the Emperors should torment and punish the Christians. Draco set downe equall punishment for manner of being the first Athenian whose decrees Solon abolished, saue onely those which were against murder. Aristotle maketh mention of a Countrey, where the inhabitants were to assure the safety of the wares, and to repay vnto passengers that losse vvhich they had sustained theeues and robbers. Aristo. de repub. Torquatus, caused his sons heade be cut off, because hee fought against hys body to body, co~trary to the Edicts out of his ranke, although he came away victory. Vectius vvas presently slaine, because not vvhen the Trybune of the people ssed before him. Fabius Maximus his sonne (beeing one of Magistrates of Rome) seeing his Father of comming towards him on horseke, and that the Sergiants in regarde of therly reuerence, had not caused him to ght, commaunded him to set foote on the ound, which the Father presently obeied, embraced his sonne, making more acunt of him then if he had done otherwise. The Poets, to declare the excellencie of this faine VVisedome to be a vvoman, and be borne of no mortall creature, but of Iupir himselfe; who~ Painters so set foorth, that on side soeuer any one beholding it dyd stand, either before her, or behinde her, hee had a sight of her. GOD inabled Salomon to dispute of hearbes and plants, euen from the Cedars in Libanus, to the Pellitorie roote groweth out of the wall. The Oracle of Apollo pronounced th the Chaldeans and the Hebrewes onely vvisedome parted betweene them. The Grecians boast, that all the vvise were of Greece. Socrates beeing (according to the iudgment of the Physiognomers) giuen to wickednes, by the study of wisedome himselfe, and became a good examp of a godly man. The wisedome of Fabius Marcellus so admired honoured of the Romans, th the one was called the Buckler, the other Sword of the Romaine Empire. Among the Romans was a Colledge of men, called Augures by whose authoritie, state vvas sometimes gouerned. Homer in the vvhole discourse of his where Minerua alwayes Vses gyueth vs to vnderstand, that ought alwayes to guide a man to aine to the end of his enterprise. Men praised the prudence of Fabius, beuse he broke the point of fortune, and the aduancement of Hanibal by cuncion, temporising, attending his aduange, which is a vertue named long suffence. Cicero. Cato, when he saw that Pompey ioyned himselfe with Caesar, told him that did put Caesars yoake vpon his necke, wh then he perceaued not, but shortly it wou weigh heauy vpon him, and then should finde himselfe taken. Themistocles, at what time he was Athence, and inforced to goe into being intreated of the King to shew estate of his Country, he wisely besought one yeare, to learne the Persian and then he would tell him. enioyned vpon paine of death, his Soueraigne, to make an Asse to knowing it a matter impossible, seauen yeares space, hoping in that time, eyther the King, he, or the Asse would die. Simonides being at a banquet with he tooke occasion to desire him to some precepts of wisedome, at which laughed, and said, Remember thou art a vvhich then he not regarded, but afterwa in his misery, with great sorrow Theophrastus. Cato, for the loue that he beare vnto widome, entertained Athenodorus, Vlisses, as saith, embraced Carylus, Pyrrhus eeemed Artemius, Traian desired Plutarch Scipio Panetius, who was learned, in all both good and euill. Euclides of Megara, desirous to heare the of Socrates, who read Philosophy Athence, betweene vvhich two Citties, ere was mortall emnity, so that no Cittin of the one durst be seene in the other, great danger disguised himselfe like woman, and so heard Socrates. Agesilaus sustaining great losses by Epamindas, commaunded his Souldiours to head against him onely, because that but wise and prudent men knew how conquer. Athenians being deuided and banded three contrary parts and factions, Solon not ioyne himselfe with any one of em, but kept him indifferent to all, seeking all meanes to reconcile them together, in end being chosen their pacifier, he their estate, and placed them in greater then before. although numbred among the sean of Greece, refused to interme in common wealth matters. Demades, a man very pollitique, and in state, being asked what Tutor he to instruct him in wisdom, answered, the trbunall of the Athenians, meaning the Cou and experience to excell all the precepts Philosophy. Antonius the meeke, was a vertuous Emperour, and so well aduised in all his that hee neuer repented him of thing he did. Romulus, the first King, founder of Citty of Rome, chose of the eldest in the same Country, by whose wisdom he willed it should be gouerned. Iulius Caesar gloried in his good fortune but yet the bringing of his great enterpri to passe, was by his wisedom and experien in warlike affaires. The Lacedemonians made more acco of an exployt done by pollicy, then by whose Captaines vvhen they had by the pollitique stratagems ouercome any, sacriced to theyr Gods an Oxe, if by force Cocke. Alexander about to destroy the Citty Lampsacus, Anaxemines his master cam him, intending to desire him to it, but the king imagining wherfore he sweare that hee vvould not graunt that Anaximines should request, who desid Alexander to destroy Lampsacus, which quest by his oath he could not graunt, and by this pollicy he saued his Citty. The Italians vnable to excuse the great ults, treacheries, cowardize, and dissimulaon of their Nation, go about to colour their llanies with the name of Italian prudence. One bought a draught of fish of certaine fiers in Milesia, whose hap was to take with theyr net a golden Tripos, which the refused to giue theyr ying, that they bargained for fish, the was brought before the Magistrates, who co~manded by the Oracle, to giue it to wisest man; first it was giuen to Thales, he it to Bias, Bias to Pittacus, vntil it came Socrates, who gaue it to Apollo. Tully cryed out in his latter age, vtinam sapuisse~ would had neuer knowne wisedome meant. Quintus Catulus did his Country as much good by his wisedome, as Cneius Pompeius by valour, for of small force is the warre vnlesse there be good aduise at home. Phillip of Macedon, being in hostage three yeares together, learned prudence of Epaminondas, by which vertue he got into hands, the monarchy of all Greece, and great part of Asia. Caesar, when he tooke vpon him, the gouernment of the Gaules, waged warre there yeares, guided by vnspeakable prudence, that was accompanied with diligence, so that by these, he subdued Townes, and in many battailes discomfited three millions of men. The Romaine Kings kept Eagles in theyr campe, against thunder and lightning. The Emperour Tiberius, wore in his Bay braunch, to keepe him from thunder lightning. The Aegiptian mariners, were wont in stomy and tempesteous weather, to hang vp saile, on the which was sewed the Phoca skinne, which is a kind of fish, called the Cowe. Alexander Seuerus was a very wise Prince, which he attained vnto, by the counsaile and instruction of that learned Lawyer Vlpianus. The Sages, or of Greece, were renowned throughout al the world, of whom the first was Thales Milesius, who inuented card to saile by. The second was Solon, who gaue the first wes to the Athenians, and iudged no man ppy before his death. The third was Chilo of Lacedemon, vvho Embassadour into the Orient for the Aenians. The fourth was Pittacus, who was not only Philosopher, but also Captaine of the Myenes. The fift was Cleobulus, that descended fro~ auntient line of Hercules. The sixt was Periander, of whom the Hioriographers doubted, whether his Philophy or tirany were greater. The seauenth Bias, that was Prince of the a learned Philosopher, and a vaant Souldiour, who ouercame the this battaile was the first that any of Greece fought. The Grecians had their Philosophers, the Persians their Magi, the Indians the Aegiptians Priests, the Hebrewes Prophets, the Assirians Chaldeans, the Lanes the Druides, vvhich in euery of these Nations, and all the world, were renowned for their wisedome and profound learning. The property of this vertue consisteth in things which belong to the keeping of mans li in his body, and vsing the pleasures thereof mderately, being a meane in our seeing, bearing smelling, tasting, and feeling. daies, when vppon mount Sinai, he was to receaue the of the law from God. Minos, as it is fayned, when he was to lawes from Iupiter, fasted nine dayes Homer Daniell and his companions, neglecting Kings table, liued with pulse and water Bib. Plato forsooke Dionysius courtly feasting betook himselfe to his philosophicall diet. Saint Iohn Baptist passed ouer the part of his age in the vvildernes, eating nothing but Locusts and wild honey. Bartholomew the Apostle, when Polemion King of India, sent him Cammels richly loaden with gold and siluer, for that he had dispossessed his daughter of an vncleane spit, refused them saying, that hee came not to ceaue rewards for his hire, but that he the way of saluation, to those that beleeue. Anacharsis the Scithian philosopher, counled Kings and Princes, to write about their ctures, Rule lust, temper the tongue, bridle the Augustus vvas of a very spare dyet, his was to sit downe to meate, when his had halfe dined, and would be the first rised. Scipio for the space of fifty foure yeares, bought nor sold any thing, he was so contented with a little. Scipio in the flower of his age, at the taking of the Citty of Carthage, had a young to his prisoner, of rare and excellent beauty, and when he vnderstood her birth, that she was betrothed to Lucius of Spain, sent for him, and restored her vnto him, without abusing her any way, besides giuing her a dowry. Alexander did the like with Darius vvife, who excelled all the dames of Asia for beauty: the like of Cyrus. Phryna the harlot, lying with vpon a wager, to proue his continency, she lay not with a man, but with a Laertius. C. Gracchus, as long as he gouerned would neuer suffer a woman to come into his house, except it vvere to iustice. Pyttacus being constrained to take him the charge of an Army, accepted it with great griefe, saying, howe hard a matter is to be a good man? Laertius. Torquatus, and Fabritius, absented themselues from Rome, the one because he not haue the dictatorship, the other the consulship. Of all those which sought the of Rome, neuer any sober man went the same but Caesar. Vespasian was of that temperance, that be would not drink nor eate, but once a day, and that very sparingly. Socrates, by his great abstinence, liued his life without sicknes. M. Val. Coruinus, liued free from sicknes, an hundred yeares by his abstinence. Massinissa King of Numidia, neuer sate at his table, neuer sawced his meate, and was ntent with that bread he allowed vnto his uldiours. when one of his minions moued him see Panthea, saying, that her beauty was worthy to be seene; that is the cause said rus, why will abstaine from the sight of Xenophon. hauing escaped the election of of those three hundred Senators, which uerned the estate of Sparta, returned ioy, saying, that it was an easie matter to find that Citty three hundred better, and more men then himselfe. Duke of Sauoy, willingly gaue or his Dutchy, into his Sonnes hands, and came an Hermit, and after that, being cho Amurath, the second of that name, after he obtayned infinite victories, became a of the straightest sect amongst them. Charles the fift, resigned his Empire into hands of the Princes Electors, and withew himselfe into a monastrey. Cato the younger, trauailing ouer the derts of Lybia, endured great thirst, when Souldiour offered him water, in his motion threw it vpon the ground, in presence of them all, that his Army might know that would be in no better estate then they. Socrates, when soeuer he felt himselfe thirsty, would not drinke before he had cast away the first pitcher of water, that he might acquaint his sensuall appetite, to expect the conuenient time of reason. The Germaines in Iulius Caesars time, a strong warlike people, liued only of milk, cheese, and flesh, not knowing what wheate and vvine were, nor vvhat it was to labor the ground, or to sowe. Liuia commendeth the barrainnes and sterility of a Country, more then the fruitfulnes saying, that men borne in a fat soile, are commonly and cowards, but the barraine Country bringeth forth temperate and sober persons; the Athenians were situated in a very vnfruitfull place. The feasts of Pythagoras, Socrates, Xenocrates, and the Sages of Greece, were the discourses of learned matters philosophy. The Aegiptians vsed in the midst of theyr banquets, to bring in the Anatomy of a dead body dried, that the horror of it might hold them within the bonds of temperance. In the old time Vines were planted and that wine might be drunk, rather in of sicknes, then of health; in so much it was not sold in Tauerns only, but also Apothicaries shops. The Emperor Rodolphus, when drink was brought vnto him in the war, against Octotarus King of Bohemia, at what time he was a place, where his whole Army was troubled with thirst, would not receaue it, but sayd, that his thirst was for all his Army, and not alone for himselfe. Pythagoras liued only of hearbs, fruit, and water, he neuer drank vvine, nor that great Orator Demosthenes. The Kings of Aegipt were forbidden vvine, which they neuer drank, except on certaine daies, and that in measure. Alexander refused the Cookes and Paysterers, which Ada Q. of Caria, sent vnto him, saying, that he had better then they, namely, For his dinner early rising, and walking a good while before day, for his supper a litle dinner but the Persian delicacies soon changed this. C. Fabritius vvas found by the Samnite Embassadors that came vnto him, eating of Rape roots, which was all the fare he had. Hanibal fed vpon no other meat, then the meanest of his Souldiers did. The Priests of Aegipt, the Sages of and Persia, and Iupiters Priests, seruing Gods, did neuer eate any flesh, nor drink vvine. Anacharsis a Seithian Phylosopher, being demaunded of his estate, how he fed, how he did lie, and how he was cloathed, aunswered, feede on hunger, lie on the ground, and am cloathed like a Scithian. Dyonisius made sute to Aristides, for his daughter in marriage, but he knowing him to be an intemperate Prince, soberly answered, that he had rather kill his daughter with his owne hand, then giue her in marriage vnto Dionysius. Valerius Publicola, after he had been consull foure times, died so poore, that he had not sufficient to defray the charge of his Funerals, but was buried of the common tresury. The ke of Menenius Agrippa, vvhen by the counsaile of Epimenides of Create, the Athenians vvere deliuered from a plague, which their neighbours were infected with, they in regard of his loue aduice, sent him rich rewards, which he refused. Apollonius Tyanaeus had diuers rich gifts sent him by Vespasian, which he would not saying, that they were for couetous minded men and for those that had neede of them. The Romaines laughed Sylla to scorne, that being a man most intemperate, did not withstanding vse to exhort, and compell others to sobriety, temperance, and frugality. Lisander contrary to him, allowed those in the Cittizens, from the which himselfe refrained. Pericles, when his companion Sophocles and Pretor in Rome, commended the of a young woman, whom they met, said, It becommeth a Pretor to haue not onely hands free from corruption, but also continent eyes, voyde of vnchast lookes. Hortensius was much reproued, for that at a supper (prepared for the Augurs) he set before them a boiled Peacock. Cassius was deemed intemperate, because publiquely he drank water, and could not for a short time endure the thirst thereof. Duronius was remoued from the Senate, for that he being Tribune, repeated the law concerning the restraint of feasting. VVhen the which King Pyrrhus, after his ouerthrow, were brought to Rome and shewed about the streetes, hoping to winne good will of the people, the was not one man seene to put out his hand towards them, so as the King found himselfe no lesse vanquished with continency, force of armes. Diogenes laughed those to scorne, that by sacrifice sought for helpe of the Gods, and notvvithstanding led an intemperate lyfe. Cato by prescribing too spare temperate dyet, killed his wife and child. In the presence of Gorgo, the daughter of Cleomenes, but yeares old, Aristagoras intreated Cleomenes, that the Lacedemonians would send an Army into Asia, promising to giue him talents, which he refusing, offered him the wench tooke her Father a side, and sayd, Father, if you get you not hence, this guest will corrupt you vvhereat he departed, without hearkning to Aristagoras any more. The Lacedemonians were very temperate in their dyet, and had certaine publique places, called Phidities where they fed, of which came, that when men would speake of a small pittance, they vvould lyke it to a meale of Phiditie The Esseans a certaine Iewish sect, vvho were holier and of better conuersation then Pharisies, abstained from wine and vvomen. The temperance and staiednes of Titus Quintus, got more countries to the Romans then al the forces vnder him had done. It was felonie for the Magistrates of Locris to drinke wine without the lycence of a and the Romans neuer drunke wine, before they were twenty yeres old. In the tyme of Saturne, the world did neyther eate flesh, nor drinke wine, wherin they agree with our Diuines, who put vs out of doubt, that the vse of flesh and wine, was vnknowne before the vniuersall flood. The vertue of the mind aduentureth nothing shly, neyther in a good cause feareth death, be in apparaunce neuer so terrible: whose extreames are feare and foolish boldnes. FOure kinds of people the Romans found hard to ouercome, the Mermidons, the Gaditanes, the Saguntines, the Numantines, the first were strong, the second valant, the third fortunate, but the Numantine were strong, valiant, and fortunate. Amongst all the Citties of the world, Numantia did neuer acknowledge her better, or kisse the hande of any other for Lord. The Lacedemonians neuer vsed to aske number of their enemies, but vvhere vvere. Iudas Macchabeus beeing begirt with thousand men, was counsailed to flie, forbid (quoth he) that the sunne should flie, had rather die then staine my glory by ignominious flight The Numantines vvhen they were besiged slew nine Consuls, vvherevpon, the Romans did capitulate with them that should be perpetuall friends. Fiue thousand resolute Romans, ouerca thirty thousande of Methridates souldio vvhom hee had chosen throughout all kingdom. Iulius Caesar, entering the Temple of Hecules in Gades, seeing the heroycall gests Alexander set forth vpon the vvalls, fell the lyke passion for Alexander, as he did hilles. Q. Mutius aduentured alone into the tents King Porsenna, eyther to kill the King, or be killed by him, for which he purchased sirname of Sceuola. Horatius Cocles resisted the whole Armie the same king, vntil the cittizens of Rome to take vp the drawe bridge, and then all armed leapt into the riuer Tyber, and escaped his enemies. Perdiccas entered into the dangerous den a Lyonesse, and tooke avvay her whelps. rtius. Starchaterus to increase his strength, fedde on Beares fleshe, and often vsed to drinke eir blood. Alexander thought himselfe happy if hee be named Achilles, Caesar if he might called Alexander; Achilles sought no name then Theseus, Theseus desired of Hercules. Although Scythia was barren yet was shee oute, though rude and barbarous, yet was very valiant, and hard to bee subdued. Leonides at Thermopyla, hauing vnder charge but foure thousand souldiours, liantly encountred with the huge Armie of Xerxes, and ouercame it, to his fame and Xerxes eternall infamie. Pyrrhus seeing the fortitude and the Romaines, sayd, If valour were lost, mould thereof might bee founde in a Romans hart; adding, that hee would quicklie conquer all the worlde if hee were King Rome, or the Romaine souldiours subiect vnto him. Solon made a law, that the children parents had beene valiantly slaine in battaile, should for the prowesse of theyr parents, euer after maintained of the Common treasurie. Lucius Dentatus was in sixescore battailes and eyghteene times came away Hee receiued in token of his valour, eyghteene Launces, twenty Bards for horses· Bracelets, and It vvas all the manner of the Lacedemonians· to be greatly inflamed with the desire conquering. Eumenes, (though neuer so distressed) thought himselfe strong enough, as long he had his sword in his hand. Aristomenes the Messenian, beeing the Lacedemonians and deliuered fast und to two souldiours, hee drew neere to fire, burned his bonds in sunder, killed his eepers, and saued himselfe. Lysimachus vvas commaunded by Alexder that he should be deuoured of a Lion, at he valiantly fought with the beast, and retching forth his arme, thrust it into hys roate, taking holde of his tongue, and so rangled him, whereupon hee vvas euer afr more esteemed of Alexander then hee before. Cassius aunswered a Chaldean Astrologer counselled him not to fight vvith the vntill the Moone had passed Scoro, feare not (quoth he) Scorpius, but feare Archers: because the Romans were put by Parthian Archers. Agis vpon the poynt to giue battaile to the ycaonians, vvhen his souldiers sayde, that eyr enemies were many; aunswered, The that will subdue many, must of necessity ght with many. Leonides beeing informed by his souldiers at the enemies against whom hee vvas to ght, vvere so many in number, that theyr darkned the beames of the sunne, much the better (quoth he) for we shall the~ fight in the shade. Alcibiades, when his Captaines suddainlie made an alarum with great citties that they were fallen into theyr enemies hands, would say vnto his souldiours, Be valiant and feare not, for we are not fallen into their hands, but they into ours. Scaeua a Iew, at the siege of Ierusalem hauing long time defended his fellow souldiers, after much slaughter by him made, abode still fighting, hauing his eyes stopped, hys body vvounded, and his shield strooke thorow in sixscore places. Iulius Caesar, perceiuing the Neruians to haue the better hand, caught a Target from out a souldiours hand that began to flie, and taking his place, did such feates of Armes, that all his Armie recouered courage, got the victory. Alexander swimmed ouer dangerous vvaters, scaled townes, and put himselfe formost in perrils and Pyrrhus, Haniball, Sertorius and Caesar, are reported to haue done the like. Eutycus beeing blinde, was set without the aray of the battaile by Leonidas; but being ashamed to leaue his companions, caused a slaue to leade him to the place vvhere they there valiantly behauing himselfe, was slaine. Sylla the Dictator, hauing condemned to all the inhabitants of Perouza, none but his hoast, he would needes saying; that he scorned to hold his lyfe of the murtherer of his country. The Polonian Ambassadors aunswered when he threatned theyr country; VVee feare (saide they) but one onely thing, which is least the skie fall vpon vs. Pompey dreadlesse of a great storme whe~ he vvas sent by the Senate into Italie, vvas the first that went a and commaunded the sailes to be spred, saying: It is necessary that goe, but not necessary that liue. Xerxes great Nauie that dranke vvhole riuers dry, vvas rather a signe of his vvealth then magnanimitie. Bias holding warres with Iphiorates, and put to the vvorst, his souldiours cryed out, saying: vvhat shall we doe? to vvhom hee aunswered, Tell those that are aliue, that dyed fighting, and will report vnto the deade, that you escaped flying. The women of Lacena vvent into the field with their husbands. Thomyris Queene of Scythia, ouercame Cyrus, cut off his head, cast it into a bowle of blood, saying; Satiate sanguine quem sitiisti. The vvomen of Scythia, called Amazons, lyued as conquerours ouer men, and vvere neuer conquered by men, vntill Alexander destroyed both them and theyr country. Semyramis, when newes was brought her that her citty Babylon vvas besieged, all vnattyred and vndressed, she tooke her armor, and by her vvonderfull valour repulsed her enemies. Zenobia, Queene of the Palmerians, after the death of her husband gouerned the Empire, and long helde battaile against the Emperour Aurelian, vvho sayd, That it was valour to conquer a woman so stoute as Zenobia, then to vanquish a king so fearefull as Xerxes Penthiselea, Queene of the Amazons, and Hyppolita, the first encountred hande to hand Achilles; the other Theseus, whom hee for her valour and courage afterward married. Artimesia Queene of Caria, after the death of her husband, shewed such admirable fortitude against the Rhodians, that she burned theyr Nauies, entered theyr Citties, and used in them her Image to bee set vp for a of her chiualrie. VVhen Epaminondas besieged Sparta, gotten into the Towne, Isadas a young all naked, his body annointed ouer oyle, hauing a partisone, thrust himselfe to the midst, beating downe all his before him, and himselfe escaped away The Ephori at his return gaue him a crown honor of his provvesse, but they amerced at a thousand crownes for beeing so The Soule is called Anima whilst it is in the and giueth lyfe, Mens while it mindeth, Animus hauing will, Ratio for that it iudgeth rightfully, Spiritus while it breatheth, Sensus whilst it feeleth. THe Soule hath fiue vertues, of the which the first is feeling, by this vertue the soule is mooued, desiring those thing that belong to the body. The second povver is vvit, by thys the soule knovveth all things, sensible and corporall, when they are present. The third is Imagination, by vvhich it the likenes of bodily thinges they be absent. The fourth is Reason, that iudgeth betweene good and euill, truth and falshood. The fift is Vnderstanding, the which comprehendeth things not materiall, but intelligible, as God and Angels. The three first virtues are situate in the soule that is coupled to the body, and giueth lyfe and inner wit to perfection of the body, and these bee common both to men and beasts. The other tvvo, Reason and Vnderstanding, be in the soule in that it may be departed from the body, and abide beeing departed, as an Angell by two manner of respects, for it beholdeth the higher things, and therevpon is called Intellectus and the lower, and for that cause is termed Ratio In diuers bodies the soule is threefold, Vegitable that is, giueth life and no feeling, as in plants and rootes, vvhich the Philosophers liken to a Tryangle in Geometry, for as that hath three corners, so hath this soule three vertues, the first begetting, the second nourishing, the third growing. that gyueth lyfe and feeling, not which is in beasts; thys soule is lyked to a Quadrangle, for it is a line drawne one corner to another before it maketh Triangles, and the sensible soule maketh triangles of vertues; for soule Sensible is, there is also the soule but not contra The Reasonable soule giueth life, feeling, reason, which is in men; this soule is kened to a circle because of her perfection containing, for of all the figures of the length, the circle is most, most and whosoeuer hath the soule Reasonable, hath also the Sensible, and Vegitable, sed non contra. The soule beeing once made, shall endure euermore in body or out of body, and that shall neuer be sayde that it vvas made by the Image of GOD, if it were closed in the bonds of death. Plato calleth the soule a beeing, which only mooueth it selfe, Zeno termeth it a number which mooueth it selfe, Pythagoras an harmony, Democritus a subtile and vncertaine spyrite, Aselepiades saith it is a manner of cord that setteth the fiue Sences a vvorke, Porphyrius, Idea Hippocrates, a subtile spirit spred through all the body, and Epicrus a kinde of fire and ayre. Pythagoras maintained Palingenesia is, that soules departed, returne into bodies; Hee sayde that hee remembred hee was Euphorbius, at the sacke of Troy. There vvas an auncient lavve vnder Saturne, that vvhen good men departed out of thys lyfe, they be sent into the fortunate Iles, vvhich Iles the Poet Pyndarus describeth, the vvicked are sent into the Iaile of vengeance, which he calleth Tartarus Plutarch imitating Plato, bringeth in Thespesias raysed from the dead, to discourse of the lyfe to come, De sera numinis vindicta The Thracians vvere sirnamed the Getes, vvho vvere of opinion, that after theyr departure out of thys vvorld, they vvent to Zamolrix or Gebelezie that is in the Getish of Goatish tongue, to him that gaue them health, saluation, and all kind of happinesse. Cleombrotus a Phylosopher, when he had reade a Treatise of the immortalitie of the soule, presently slew himselfe, so did Cato of Vtica. That which Virgill sayth in his second Eggue, concerning the drugge or spice of called Amomum and the going thereof vvhere, is of some interpreted to bee of the immortalitie of the soule, the wherof Pherecides brought thence to Greece, that it should bee vnderstoode the vvorld. The taking of Enoch into heauen of God, doone that the vvorlde might thereby and beleeue, that there is after this lyfe. The Indians burne themselues before they to extreame age, terming it the letting of men loose, and the freeing of the soule fro~ the body, and the sooner they did it, the vviser they vvere esteemed. Zeno sayd, that he had rather see an Indian burne himselfe cheerefully, then to heare all the Phylosophers of the vvorlde discoursing the immortality of the soule. The people that dwell by the riuer Niger, otherwise called the people of Seneca in Affrica, offer themselues vvith great willingnes to bee buried quicke with their maisters; vvherevpon Zeno sayd, that all the demonstrations of Logicke and Mathematick, had not so much force to proue the immortality of the soule, as this onely deed of theirs. Alexander asked a Gymnosophist, there were more men aliue then deade he sayd there were more aliue, because no are dead. All the learning of the Sages Scythians, was grounded vppon the immortality of the soule. The Schollers of Hegesias hearing there Maister discoursing of the immortalitie of soules departed out of thys lyfe, vvere so rauished with his words, that they vvillinglie killed themselues. The soules of Saints in heauen, knowe nothing vvhat is doone vpon the earth; for if they did, said August: my mother Monicha would bee with mee euery night, to comfort me in my heauines. de ciuit. Plinie the elder, denying the immortalitie of the soule, vvhilst hee was ouer curious in searching out the cause of the burning Aetna was burned therein. iust punishment for him, to end his life by smoake, who esteemed the soule no better then a vapour. Origen attributeth vnto the soules departed, a place vpon the earth, where they learn those thinges which they knewe not vvhile they liued; As the Papists frame a Purgatorie, so he an Eruditory. Philoronimus a priest of Galatia, liued sixe eres in dead mens vaults and Sepulchers, at bee might alwayes remember, that hee dead to the vvorld, and aliue to Christ. Pope commanded two Phylosophers discourse of the soule, the one to proue immortalitie, the other that it was and when the Pope was to giue hee sayde to him that had maintained immortality, Thou hast argued the truth, the reasons of the other sauour of more pleare and liberty. The soules of Tyrants are composed of arogancie and cruelty.
